Subject: [Ilugc] Ubuntu or Debian
In-Reply-To: <c245550405072903012affb58c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <c245550405072903012affb58c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <5d0d0e310507312131e9d7843@mail.gmail.com>

On 7/29/05, Shuveb Hussain <shuveb@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hi,
> 
> I have been a Gentoo user for a few years now and I have been
> comfortable. At work, I recently switched to Ubuntu. It has been
> great. But since there are experienced Debian users in the group, I
> ask you this:
> 
> Do I have reasons to choose Debian over Ubuntu?
> Do I have reasons to choose Debian over Ubuntu?

I don't know what your priorities are but I do have reaons to  choose
Ubuntu over debian.
It has latest of the packages included. Though much of the work is
based on the debian
base, things are changing now. Xorg for instance was first included in
ubuntu and is now
being ported to debian. Ubuntu is very much focused on security.
Though many people say
that it is focused on desktop and novice users there is no reason why
an experienced users
shouldn't use it, especially when you can get the work done with
lesser effort. All the packages needed for me is in the Ubuntu repos,
If at all I find a package not in the Ubuntu there is always the
debian packages as a fall back.

guidelines. Please don't reply to this e-mail.

- There are lot of people top-posting in this mailing

- Disclaimers are not encouraged in this mailing list.

> wrote:
> > 
> > I want to know where can i buy ADSL modems in
> chennai, for a good deal...
> > any address, model name, etc... i tried in richie
> street but they were

I think we should put up a webpage on Ritchie Street
in our wiki site with the different _trusted_ shops
where we buy our stuff. 

I go to Sagar Infosystems. There is a guy called
Vinod, there. Recently, he had a problem with a small
Sony Vaio portable computer that had come from Japan.
As usual windoze crashed ... what else can you
expect?. 

Someone suggested booting from some windoze boot disk,
use fdisk, but, it didn't lead him to anything. I told
him to boot from some floppy GNU/Linux distribution to
test the hardware. It only booted from a small hard
disk or through floppy. He got hal91 from the link
here:

http://www.linuxlinks.com/Distributions/Floppy/
 
and while boot up, during hard disk read/write he got
the status ready read error. I told him hard disk
problem, and it had to be changed. He was now
confident to answer the client. Case closed.

SK

Yes, go to http://192.168.1.1/ in your browser with the modem on (of
course!) and the log in as user: admin password: admin

You can change the properties of the router from the web interface. I
dont think port forwardind on port 21 (FTP) is possible in these makes>
also check out the Dataone forum at http://vinuthomas.com for more
information
>

On 8/2/05, Sivasankar Chander <siva.ilugc@gmail.com> wrote:

> HCL uses RHEL and pays the appropriate fees to RedHat.

HCL or anyone else may redistribute free software with freedom.  RHEL
does respect this basic freedom, and merely asks the redistributor to
remove its trademarks while redistributing rhel, and the rhel
agreement makes this abundantly clear under these two terms:

<quote>
1. The Software. Red Hat Enterprise Linux and Red Hat Applications
(the "Software") are either a modular operating system or application
consisting of hundreds of software components. The end user license
agreement for each component is located in the component's source
code. With the exception of certain image files identified in Section
2 below, the license terms for the components permit Customer to copy,
modify, and redistribute the component, in both source code and binary
code forms. This agreement does not limit Customer's rights under, or
grant Customer rights that supersede, the license terms of any
particular component.

2. Intellectual Property Rights. The Software and each of its
components, including the source code, documentation, appearance,
structure and organization are owned by Red Hat and others and are
protected under copyright and other laws. Title to the Software and
any component, or to any copy, modification, or merged portion shall
remain with the aforementioned, subject to the applicable license. The
"Red Hat" trademark and the "Shadowman" logo are registered trademarks
of Red Hat in the U.S. and other countries. This agreement does not
permit Customer to distribute the Software using Red Hat's trademarks.
Customer should read the information found at
ttp://www.redhat.com/about/corporate/trademark/ before distributing a
copy of the Software, regardless of whether it has been modified. If
Customer makes a commercial redistribution of the Software, unless a
separate agreement with Red Hat is executed or other permission
granted, then Customer must modify any files identified as
"REDHAT-LOGOS" and "anaconda-images" to remove all images containing
the "Red Hat" trademark or the "Shadowman" logo. Merely deleting these
files may corrupt the Software.

</quote>

The above gives freedom to redistribute rhel, and removing the
trademark image files is a task only for someone very anxious to
redistribute this particular distro.  There is never any question of
paying royalty for free software.  Assuming HCL/any_user has purchased
a subscription to RHEL, they are free to redistribute respecting the
above condition wrt trademark images, without paying any fees/royalty.
  
> Otherwise, it is still piracy, and they're no better than the assemblers
> who include an unauthorized copy of XP with their systems. I hope HCL
> has the good sense to do the right thing here - it costs next to nothing to
> do the right thing here, and set a good example.

"Piracy" is commonly abused to refer to copyright infringements, but
in any case here, there could be "trade mark" infringement at the
worst, *if* there is any such redistribution of free software using RH
trademarks without their permission.  AFAIK, HCL is an OEM Partner of
RH, and even if people do ask for RHEL "support" - that should be
fairly easy to provide: RHEL subscription starts at around $6 per
month (Rs. 260) and should be no big deal to some one spending 9990 +
1250 on the hardware alone.  But all said, I seriously doubt if RHEL
is there in this picture at all.

I don't think you even need to be a licensed owner. You can just

The "license" of RHEL is not a license to use the software, but a

to use their PC for checking/sending e-mails, browsing the
internet, playing music and stuff, this processor is just fine.
Just that you can't expect to enjoy Quake3 Arena or Half Life at
high resolutions and higher fps on it.

question is pretty vague.

	<654433ee0508022347d14027d@mail.gmail.com>
	<op.suxbgzgfv8spko@localhost.localdomain>

On 8/3/05, Chandrashekar Babu <lug@chandrashekar.info> wrote:
> On Wed, 03 Aug 2005 12:17:15 +0530, Shiva KM <kmshiva@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
> >> VIA Processor 1 Ghz
> >
> > Hmmm.. I havent heard of this processor much - is this thesame as the
> > Cyrix processor of many years ago??
> 
> Yes. Now the processor comes from VIA.
> 
   The processor is *not* the same, although Via bought/licensed the IP core
of the Cyrix 6x86MX or M2 core, for some of the early Via C3 CPUs.
(The last processor built by Cyrix was an MMX Socket-7 CPU called the MII, 
comparable to a Pentium 233/MMX. Clock-for-clock, this is still the highest
performance x86 CPU ever built, but it never scaled beyond 300 MHz or so,
before Cyrix was acquired by National Semiconductor.)

   National Semiconductor then used the Cyrix M2 core in a line of embedded
x86 CPUs called the MediaGX and later the Geode. This line of
CPUs was later sold to AMD, which has enhanced the range with several
Athlon-core embedded x86 processors at clock speeds of over 1 GHz, consuming
a few Watts of power. These Geode NX CPUs are not pin-compatible with any
other consumer x86 CPUs, and require special motherboards to use them.
They're mostly used in embedded boxes, including Firewalls, Routers, SANs,
etc.

OTOH, the Via CPUs contain a core from Centaur Technology, which built
an excellent
low-power, small-die core family. The 1st generation of that core was a Socket-7
CPU called the Winchip, followed by the Winchip II. Both these came to market
too late to make an impact on the Socket-7 market, which was being phased
out by that time. However, the 3rd-generation Centaur core was used by
Via in a line of Socket-370 CPUs (compatible with the Celeron/PIII) called 
the Cyrix III (to indicate compatibility with the PIII socket-370). Apart from
the name, the CPU has nothing in common with the Cyrix M2 cores. IMHO, the
Via Cyrix III/C3 is an excellent performer at its price point - it
retailed for $15 when
the least expensive Celerons cost about $50, and easily blew away the Celerons
on most memory-intensive benchmarks, although they were only about half as 
fast on floating-point.

   The latest generation of the Via/Centaur CPUs is a Socket-478 (P4-compatible)
CPU that runs at up to 2 GHz, and uses a fraction of the power of the P4. It's
the most interesting Socket-478 CPU available, in that it has a HW cryptographic
coprocessor on the die. (Eventually, the Linux kernel CryptoAPI will support HW
acceleration.)

> > I had an old compaq machine with a Cyrix MediaGX processorwith a rating
> > of 133MHz, but actually ran at 100MHz or 90MHzor something - performance
> > wasn't very good though...
>
    The MediaGX was from National Semiconductor (see above), and was an
embedded x86 CPU, meant for set-top boxes, routers and the like. It was
never meant to be a desktop CPU, though that did not prevent some companies
from building low-end consumer desktops around it. These were mostly destined
for price-sensitive markets, and they were never meant to compete on
performance.

   The MediaGX has nothing in common with the Via C3 CPUs - the C3 is an
excellent performer for the price. Try a C3/733 to get an idea of the capability
of the Centaur core.
 
> 
> Just that you can't expect to enjoy Quake3 Arena or Half Life at
> high resolutions and higher fps on it.
> 
    I'd be perfectly happy to get a $15 Geforce4 MX card and use
the latest generation socket-478 Via CPU for gaming. I'd give even
odds that this will blow away an Intel CPU on an Intel integrated-
graphics motherboard like the i845/865/915 at a small fraction
of the cost.

   If you want high frame-rates, invest in a good GPU instead of
an expensive CPU. An inexpensive CPU + inexpensive but
good previous-gen GPU, can easily outperform a top-end CPU +
a crappy integrated graphics combination, at a fraction of the
cost.

-Siva

On 8/3/05, Parthan S R <parth_srp@yahoo.com> wrote:
> 
> I have RH9 in my PC, is there ane way to upadte/change
> it to RHEL ,by means of downloading certain stuffs
> from the net ? If so, plz enlighten me on the same!
> 
   In principle, you can download RHEL SRPMs and rebuild
them and install them. These, however, will not yield exactly
the same binaries as RHEL, unless they're built on a RHEL
system. You'll have a chicken-and-egg problem, which can take
a lot of work to resolve dependencies and bootstrap it
successfully (it's pretty hard to even bootstrap from RH9
to FC1 from SRPMs alone, leave alone RH9 to RHEL).

  Notwithstanding the enormity of the task, this has actually
been done by a number of people who have come out with
distros like Centos, WBEL, CERN Scientific Linux, Trustix,
etc.

-Siva

Contaminating Free Software with trademarks or other proprietary
images are unwarranted and none can claim it as a right. From a strict
point of view, RH could be seen as violating the GPL, but, taking into
view its other substantial and generous contributions, probably many
would take only a very light view of the practice.

need, to save time, labour and for many other reasons.  I do not know
what understanding prevails in the US, but atleast here, "service
contracts" are very well understood and those desiring to earn revenue
through support, should seriously think of plainly marketing "Service
Contracts".  Eureka Forbes has done a good job of educating people
about service contracts for vacuum cleaners/water filters through door
to door campaigns, and the nuances of a service contract are very well
understood here.  The Indian market is vast, and the opportunities are
many - enough to feed many a Goose ;)

Links to the archives:

Possible Red Hat GPL Violation

http://lists.gpl-violations.org/pipermail/legal/2005-March/000049.html

The onerous conditions requiring licensees to remove their propreitary
stuff before redistribution are needless and certainly against the
terms and spirit of the GPL.  I'll take Siva's word that the task is
not an easy one, and such terms/devices to curb redistribution are
plainly violative of the GPL and against the very  spirit of our
movement.

RH has made significant contributions to the free software movement,
and that makes it more difficult to understand the rationale behind
the RHLE practice: they contradict themselves here.
From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Aug  3 21:40:05 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Aug  3 21:41:12 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Fwd: LJ Tech Tip
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0508032137200.11422-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Tech Tip from LJ :-

When writing a program that plays audio using gstreamer, make sure to
use the user's configured output method, which could be OSS, ALSA or a
sound daemon such as ESD or JACK. You don't need to look up the user's
preference, simply make a "gconfaudiosink" and set your player's audio
sink to it, for example, where the variables "sink" and "play" are
both pointers to GstElement:

 sink = gst_element_factory_make("gconfaudiosink", "sink");
 play = gst_element_factory_make("playbin", "play");
 g_object_set (G_OBJECT (play), "audio-sink", sink, NULL);

For more info on developing applications with gstreamer, see the
GStreamer documentation:
http://gstreamer.freedesktop.org/documentation/.

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

If I remember correctly, the task is ridiculously easy. All it takes
is to dump the CD into local filesystem, remove the offending packages
(there are two - redhat-logos & anaconda-images), rebuild
base/comps.xml (I think just remove the lines that refer to these two
packages) and base/hdlist (tools to build this file are included in
the anaconda package), and recreate the ISO file. The procedure is
entirely similar to adding non-Redhat RPM packages to a Redhat
installation CD and is documented all over the net.

and spirit of the GPL.

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Aug  3 22:56:21 2005

Date: Wed Aug  3 22:57:29 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (INSTALL)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0508032151270.11422-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Prof. KalyanaKrishnan R and his team (IIT-Madras) done a wonderful
job to implement the MultiLingual Indian systems.  
URL: http://acharya.iitm.ac.in/

One Day One Command 
===================

install -- Copy files and set attributes.

Summary:

'install' will copy single/multiple source(s) to destination, sets
permission modes & owner/group and take backup of existing files. It
is very useful for writing the install scripts.

Examples:

$ install myfile Dir1 -- Copy myfile to Dir1 with same name.

$ install myfile test -- Copy myfile to test.

$ install -b myfile test -- Copy myfile to test. If test is already 
                            exists, then take a backup (test~).

$ install -b -S.bak myfile test -- Same as above. But backup file will 
                                  created with .bak suffix (test.bak).

$ install --backup=t myfile test -- Take numbered backups (test.~1~).

$ install -p myfile test -- Preserve the access and modification time, 
                            while copying the file.

$ install -m 444 myfile test -- Copy myfile with specified permission 
                                mode. Default is 755.

$ install -g newgrp myfile test -- Copy myfile and set GID is newgrp.

$ install -s mybin test.bin -- Strip the symbol tables from installed 
                               binary executables.

Read: man install

Bye :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

On 8/3/05, Chandrashekar Babu <lug@chandrashekar.info> wrote:
> 
> This inspires me to rehaul my old VIA C3/733MHz box :-)
> 
> Which motherboard would you recommend to go with
> VIA C3/733 MHz to get the best performance ? Currently,
> I have an ASUS CUSI-FX board (SIS 630e chipset) and I find
> it too slow for desktop usage when compared to my Compaq
> Deskpro 4000 series (Pentium II/233 MHz machines).
> 

   I've used a Biostar M6VLA (Via PLE133 with integrated
Trident Blade graphics) with good results, but not for gaming.
This is a relatively inexpensive low-end board that's widely
available locally. It is excellent for day-to-day desktop use
and is rock stable with Redhat 7.3, and I've built two boxes 
with this combo (one for a friend, and one for myself). It's
possible to build a fanless box with this combo if you use a
heavy Thermaltake heatsink and/or underclock it to 100 FSB.

  However, it lacks an AGP slot, so you'll have to use a PCI
graphics accelerator if you want to try it out for gaming. I
believe that there's some supply of GeForce2 MX boards
for about Rs.1250 available, but YMMV.

  The other alternative is to use a Shuttle FV24/FV25 in
a small form-factor (SFF) box like the Shuttle SV-24. These
are not available locally, but it's one of the smallest
footprint full-featured x86 boxes ever built.

-Siva
From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Thu Aug  4 10:39:53 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Thu Aug  4 10:40:08 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] glibc 2.3.3 on redhat 8
In-Reply-To: <42F14F43.1080103@gmail.com>
References: <42F14F43.1080103@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a8f9901205080322096c22a4fa@mail.gmail.com>

On 8/4/05, sathish subramanian <sathish.subramanian@gmail.com> wrote:
> I have redhat 8 and want to install glic 2.3.3
> 
> what should i do ?
> 
> I searched pbone.net bu couldnt find an rpm for rh8
> 
   You can install the FC3 glibc-2.3.3 RPMs, but you'll break userland and
leave the system in a semi-usable state. The main issue is that rpm will
also break, and until you restore rpm, you won't be able to install/remove
packages. I've done this upgrade successfully for RH 7.3, and I'll post
the basic sequence of steps in due course after I'm convinced that it
it's reasonably foolproof.

   The simplest alternative is simply to do an upgrade installation of FC3 -
this takes care of all the dependency resolution automatically. The main
downside is that it messes up the GUI and so on - but most of this
can be taken care off by performing custom package selection before the
upgrade.

-Siva

On 8/3/05, Binand Sethumadhavan <binand@gmail.com> wrote:
> On 03/08/05, Ramanraj K <ramanraj.k@gmail.com> wrote:
> > We are only concerned if we can freely redistribute free software
> > without modifications, and not concerned with iso's or other packaging
> > material.  The RHEL license clearly imposes onerous conditions
> > requiring the licensee to make modifications to the software before
> > redistribution, and the following clause does not save the violation.
> 
> RHEL does not require the licensee to make modifications to software -
> what modifications are you talking about, to which piece of software
> included in RHEL? The source code is redistributable without
> encumbrances. I really can't understand what the problem is with that.
> None of the terms of the GPL or any other license is being violated
> here.

Suppose X has paid and duly obtained RHEL from RH, X should be free to
simply redistribute, say gcc binaries he has now received from RHEL to
third parties under the terms of the GPL.  RH has imposed conditions
that say that redistibution should not be done without removing its
trademarks.  In the first place, why should X be searching and nit
picking  proprietary contaminations RH has introduced?  That very
condition is onerous and clearly violates the GPL.  Further, supposing
RH trademarks are embedded into gcc binaries, that will totally
prevent X from redistributing the gcc binaries he has received from
RH.

> I'm curious what your take on SuSE Enterprise Linux is.

I was using SuSE (7.0 Professional) for more than 5 years, and I would
rank it as the best distro I have used so far.  YaST did a wonderful
job of detecting devices, installing, configuring software. YaST was
plainly proprietary then, but now it is released under the GPL. The
SuSE box included one dvd with 1600 applications, and well written
documentation. I could say this much about SuSE.

I really don't know what is so special about the "Enterprise" - I'll
update as soon as I get to it ;)

> condition is onerous and clearly violates the GPL.  Further, supposing
> RH trademarks are embedded into gcc binaries, that will totally
> prevent X from redistributing the gcc binaries he has received from
> RH.

This is your misconception. There are no Redhat trademarks embedded
into gcc binaries. If there were, then Redhat would be in violation of
the GPL.

On 04/08/05, Narayanamoorthy Srinivasan <narayanamoorthys@gmail.com> wrote:
> Dear Linux Guys,
>     I require MySQL 4.1 and PHP 5 for testing purpose in RHEL 3. I got
> MySQL 4.1 RPMS for RHEL 3 from mysql website.
>    But I have PHP version 4.3.2. I need to upgrade to PHP 5. Is PHP 5
> RPMs available for download or need to compile from PHP source.
>    How to create RPM from PHP source.
>    Even PHP 4.4 is also enough for me. I need RPMs since I feel
> maintenance is easy.

RHEL typically will not release a different major release of a piece
of software. If it started with PHP4, you will get only PHP4 for its
entire lifetime. I consider this a good thing :)

You can try rebuilding the SRPMs from Rawhide. The ones you are
looking for are available at:

ftp://download.fedora.redhat.com/pub/fedora/linux/core/development/SRPMS/php-5.0.4-10.3.src.rpm
ftp://download.fedora.redhat.com/pub/fedora/linux/core/development/SRPMS/mysql-4.1.12-2.src.rpm

Binand

On 8/4/05, Ramanraj K <ramanraj.k@gmail.com> wrote:

> SuSE box included one dvd with 1600 applications, and well written
> documentation. I could say this much about SuSE.

I think the GPL requires that you do not include proprietary binaries
in the same distribution media. One is free to distribute such
binaries in a separate media (CD/DVD) and they can even  be packaged
along with GPLed binaries containing CD/DVD in the same box. So if
Suse is distributing propreitary binaries along with other GPL code in
a single DVD, they are the ones who are violating the GPL!!

mano

From lug at chandrashekar.info  Fri Aug  5 11:04:29 2005
From: lug at chandrashekar.info (Chandrashekar Babu)
Date: Fri Aug  5 11:04:51 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] hai
In-Reply-To: <9b9414710508042212c967554@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9b9414710508042212c967554@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <op.su0sfrtwv8spko@localhost.localdomain>

On Fri, 05 Aug 2005 10:42:13 +0530, ANANTH MM <ananth.mm@gmail.com> wrote:

> my name is ananth and i am relatively new to linux and this group.

Welcome aboard!

> i am really eager to learn more on linux(though i have worked onlinux, i  
> am not that techy as you people are). where should i startfrom. what  
> books or websites would you suggest for me.

I would recommend the following site to start with:
     http://www.icon.co.za/~psheer/book/index.html.gz

Then, you can browse through online documentation (or download them)
 from the following website:
     http://www.tldp.org/


The following books are a few good ones that I recommend (if you
want to learn Linux not inclined to a specific distro, i.e.):

     * Linux Administration Handbook (the green book)
         - Evi Nemeth, Garth Snyder and Trent R. Hein.

     * Running Linux (an O'Reilly series book)
         - Matt Welsh, Matthias Kalle Dalheimer and Lar Kaufman.

     * Linux Power tools (Sybex publishers)
         - Roderick w. Smith.

Search for the above titles on amazon.com to know more. Of course,
there are many more good books and excellent websites that others
would recommend :-).

Good luck!

--
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

Try this:
download the tamil font from the site.
copy it in /usr/lib/X11/fonts/TTF
run the command "mkfontdir"
restart xfs "service xfs restart"

this worked for me on dinamani site.

wishes.

dear,
T.Shrinivasan.

> I also request others in this list who use BSNL broadband,  to help to
> check if they are able to access http://thamizha.com and
> http://mugunth.tamilblogs.com websites from your end.

I am also a DataOne BBand user. I also, face the same problem of
timeout when connecting to
http://thamizha.com &
http://mugunth.tamilblogs.com

I checked out with Ethereal Packet capture, and found that the packet
crosses my interface. When i ping, I get their IP address to be

70.85.187.98

for both sites. There is no name resolving problem. I checked with
megaproxy.com and find that there is  no problem in accessing these
sites. So, It has to be a problem at the Gateway, which is filtering
this IP or something like that.

When i tried with nmap. It gave the following msg,

All 1660 scanned ports on laurier.genwebhost.com (70.85.187.98) are: filtered
Too many fingerprints match this host to give specific OS details

See the name of the site it indicates.
laurier.genwebhost.com

Once again I get timeout when connecting to that site. But, when I
visited genwebhost.com, it gave me a test page, indicating that they
have installed TLS/SSL. This site runs on Apache server with modSSL.
So, the problem can be at DataOne gateway or at the filtered Server .

 

V.Vishnu

On 05/08/05, Benedict Herold <benedictherold@gmail.com> wrote:
>  Just tried to read about other options... While doing a search I found that
> even other alternatives too have the vulnerabilities... such as Simple
> Machine Forums, Invision Power Board... may be i've missed out some others?

You still don't get it. It is not a question of having vulnerabilities
- as you said, every non-helloworld program will have some. The
question is about the developers' receptiveness to vulnerabilities,
their speed in fixing them and their acceptance of secure coding
standards. phpBB has failed in all these counts so far, in the opinion
of a lot of people who know about these things.

Binand

browser and it is being made available for testing purposes only. Deer
Park Alpha 2 is intended for web application developers and our
testing community. Current users of Mozilla Firefox 1.0.x should not
use Deer Park Alpha 2.

Subject: [Ilugc] Firefox Problem Found 1.0.6
Message-ID: <dc538c3f05080601422a65fe00@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

For those who have webpage not downloading in firefox, its because of
your profiles might be corrupted. if you are using Firefox on Windows
XP/ windows 2000 then go to
C:\Documents and Settings\[useraccount]\Application Data and delete
the folder firefox directory under mozilla.

for those who are using windows 98 delete all the files related to the
firefox, but take a back of plugins, components, extensions folder
back up.

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Sun Aug  7 13:41:27 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Sun Aug  7 13:41:35 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Free Software User Groups in Colleges
Message-ID: <f480bf1e05080701117276232f@mail.gmail.com>

Yesterday,  there  was  a   FOSS  Awareness  Program  at  Shri  Sairam
Engineering  College, Chennai,  for 3rd  year students,  and I  gave a
short  talk  on Free  Software  User Groups  as  member  of ILUGC  and
FSF-India.  The  Principal of the College was  very enthusiastic about
the NRC  plans and  highlighted the self-employment  possibilities and
other  opportunities  available  with  free software.   Less  than  10
students knew about Gnu/Linux OS, and  much less had even heard of RMS
or Linus Torvalds.  At the end,  about half of them raised their hands
when asked if  they would opt for the FOSS  Elective the next semester
:)

I wish  NRC could  organise these awareness  programs on the  style of
LDD's organised by ilugc as one day events more like an open house for
one and all,  including the public also.  Notes about  one such LDD is
at:    http://www.chennailug.org/meeting/minutes/yr2004/momlf2004.html
and the archives have more such stories.

If there is atleast one  Free Software User Group, in each Engineering
College, it could benefit many. 

Rick Moen  has written  an excellent and  useful user group  HOWTO at:
http://www.linux.org/docs/ldp/howto/User-Group-HOWTO.html

<quote>
"[The] movement has no central structure, bureaucracy, or other entity
to direct its  affairs. While this situation has  advantages, it poses
challenges  for  allocation of  human  resources, effective  advocacy,
public relations, user education, and training."
</quote>

Again,

<quote>
Linux works precisely  because people are free to come  and go as they
please:   Free  programmers  are   happy  programmers   are  effective
programmers.
</quote>

Academic freedom and coding  freedom make good companions. User Groups
when  organised  in  Colleges  maintaining  the core  essence  of  the
movement, it could solve many other problems too:

-Education would become directly relevant to needs in society
-Enables life-long continuity for students to update themselves
-Better interaction with Public is possible
-Knowledge based societies would become a reality

That apart, many colleges are  using proprietary packages and there is
a need  to replace existing  proprietary software with  free software.
Let us please have a wiki page at ILUGC to list "equivalents".  HTH.  

Thanks,
Ramanraj.

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Sun Aug  7 19:44:49 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Sun Aug  7 19:44:58 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] FOSS Projects from India
Message-ID: <f480bf1e0508070714473aae7b@mail.gmail.com>

Frederick Noronha has compiled a list of on going FOSS Projects from India at:
http://www.iosn.net/country-reports/india

<quote>
INDIA: THERE'S A LOT HAPPENING, BUT CAN IT BE CHANNELISED?
Compiled by Frederick Noronha

India, with its population of one-billion plus, has a rich tech talent,
considerable interest in Free and Open Source Software (FOSS), and a network
of some 80-plus user groups across its landmass (some active, some less).
This offers wide potential....
</quote>

About UNDP, APDIP, IOSN:
The International Open Source Network  is an initiative of the United
Nations Development Programme's (UNDP) Asia Pacific Development
Information Programme (APDIP) and supported by the International
Development Research Centre (IDRC) of Canada.

The International Open Source Network (IOSN) is a Center of Excellence
for FOSS in the Asia-Pacific Region. It shapes its activities around
Free/Open Source Software (FOSS) technologies and applications. Via a
small secretariat, the IOSN is tasked specifically to facilitate and
network FOSS advocates and human resources in the region. The vision
is that developing countries in the Asia-Pacific Region can achieve
rapid and sustained economic and social development by using
affordable yet effective FOSS ICT solutions to bridge the digital
divide.

More details at: http://www.iosn.net/

> P.S <quote> "siva and ramanraj might remember me :)" --viyyer </quote> ;-)

Vivek, on behalf  of Sarai, attended the UoM  workshop on TRIPs Treaty
at Chennai. He gave a picture of the movement in Delhi. I also had the
opportunity to  meet Ravikanth  & Arthi from  Sarai at  the Trivandrum
FSFS meet.  A  lot of useful work is done by  Sarai to promote serious
studies touching upon the social dimensions of free software.

<quote from http://www.sarai.net/freesoftware/freesoftware.htm>
The  free  exchange of  code,  information  and  cultural products  is
central to our conception of  the digital public domain. In societies,
where hierarchy,  inequality and  control influence the  production of
ideas, a free software culture is worth fighting for.
</quote>

If  you   are  a  student,  interested  in   researching  say  "Kiosks
vs. PDA's", probably Sarai is one of the best places in India for such
studies. ( http://www.sarai.net/community/student_stipend.htm )

More info at: http://www.sarai.net

to install correctly.

From cyborg4k at yahoo.com  Mon Aug  8 00:49:15 2005
From: cyborg4k at yahoo.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Mon Aug  8 13:19:32 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [Photos] FLOSS Road Show,
	Bannari Amman Institute of Technology, Sathyamangalam
Message-ID: <20050808074915.29194.qmail@web50210.mail.yahoo.com>

Greetings!

I would like to thank Hariram Aatreya for the
opportunity given to me to accompany Murali,
Chandrasekhar, and Venkatesh from the AU-KBC center,
Madras Institute of Technology for the FLOSS road show
to Bannari Amman Institute of Technology,
Sathyamangalam, Tamil Nadu, India on August 6, 2005. 

The faculty, management and students were very much
interested in GNU/Linux, and are planning to start a
GLUG and increase their activities with GNU/Linux.
Representatives from 7 different colleges in and
around Sathyamangalam had also come for the workshop.

On the way back we checked out the FLOSS lab at Kongu
Engineering College, Erode and the projects they had
been working on. I must thank them for staying back
till 8 in the night as we finished late in the evening
at Bannari Amman Institute of Technology. 

Kongu Engineering College LUG started with 6 members
in 2003, and it has now grown to 170 members from all
the departments. They meet every week. A former
student (just graduated), Arvind Kalyan, was
responsible for taking the initiative in 2003.
Professors (like Prof. Jayapathi, HOD, CSE department)
and the management provided the support for the FOSS
activities, and continue to do so. The juniors are now
continuing the tradition :). They have also agreed to
collaborate with Bannari Amman Institute of Technology
for FOSS projects. Hopefully, KEC's mailing list will
be up and running soon.

You can view the photos of the trip and the workshop
from here:

http://www.shakthimaan.com/Mambo/gallery/album14

I request those people who are conducting workshops to
kindly update the details here:

http://www.chennailug.org/wiki/Events

Best regards,

SK

NRCF-FOSS at AU-KBC MIT organised a FOSS awarness session in Jaya
Engg College,Thirunindravur,Chennai.

I spoke on behalf of ILUGC, about Opensource,Linux and LUG.

The response was very good, especially question answer session which
lasted about 45 minutes. The college already has a functioning LUG
for nearly 3 months now. They are in the process of setting up a FOSS
lab with 60systems. 

The students and faculty are very enthusiastic about open source.

About 250 students attended the seminar.

Prof.Ramanan from AU-KBC answered many questions and also spoke about
the benefit to student in doing projects on FOSS.

Ms.Padmapriya and Senthil Anand of FOSS Centre did the intro to FOSS
and the proposed elective subject.

Thanks to NRCF-FOSS.


Raman.P

    I thank the management and the engineers at the Trioz
Technologies, Coimbatore for giving me an opportunity to take a
training session on the above mentioned field.

    Among other nifty details, the following major areas were covered:
nfsroot and cross development on targets such as x86 and ARM with
relevance to embedded systems - including tools and libraries needed.

    Though I didn't go into the specifics of ARM, they were quick
enough to bring up a x86 target themselves; these new recruits were
purely embedded people with very little exposure to Linux at any
level. I am sure that after being exposed to Embedded Linux they now
have more options at their disposal.

    The programme was for 7 days with 10 hours a day (Morning 7am to
evening 5pm) officially.

    As a sidenote, they had some nice boards down there and I was
trying my best to get my hands dirty - variations of ARM/PPC cores.

From bhuvaneswaran at gmail.com  Tue Aug  9 12:23:47 2005
From: bhuvaneswaran at gmail.com (Bhuvaneswaran A)
Date: Tue Aug  9 12:24:02 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] unable to activate java in Moilla web browser
In-Reply-To: <20050809062406.31703.qmail@web31909.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <20050809062406.31703.qmail@web31909.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <4dc6c90405080823531e8622e0@mail.gmail.com>

> is successfully installed without any errors. But i
> don't know how to activate the java. I have install

java:
You should link libjavaplugin_oji.so to plugins sub-dir under mozilla
installation. For example, if you have installed mozilla-firefox at
/usr/lib/mozilla-firefox, you should copy this .so to
/usr/lib/mozilla-firefox/plugins/ dir.

If you wish to enable it to a particular user alone, link it to
$HOME/.mozilla/plugins dir. Alternatively, you can copy the .so file
to the plugins dir. Finally, you should restart mozilla-firefox to
enable it.

flash:
If i remember right on top of my head, there is an extension which
would install libflashplayer.so to $HOME/.mozilla/plugins dir. Google
for more details.

-- 
Regards,
Bhuvaneswaran A

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Aug  9 20:28:59 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Aug  9 20:28:41 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (CDECL)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0508091950490.5858-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Mr Pramod CE and his team developed a Phoenix Live CD for Physics with
Homemade Equipment and Innovative Experiments. Now this project is
maintained by NSC New Delhi. URL: http://www.nsc.res.in/~elab/phoenix/

One Day One Command 
===================

cdecl -- Create/Explain C Type Declarations.

Summary:

Cdecl is a program for encoding and decoding C type declarations in
English language. It can run in interactive (shell-like) and
non-interactive mode (command line arguments).

In the interactive mode, cdecl will wait for your input in "cdecl> " 
prompt. Enter "quit or exit" to exit. Enter "?" for help.

Examples:

$ cdecl -- Start the cdecl in interactive mode.

cdecl> quit -- Exit cdecl.

cdecl> declare i as static integer 

cdecl> declare p as extern pointer to int

cdecl> declare p as array of int

cdecl> declare fun as function returning void

cdecl> declare _exit as function (retvalue as int) returning void

cdecl> explain int **p

cdecl> explain int *p[]

cdecl> explain void (*signal())()

cdecl> explain int (*f)()

cdecl> cast i into char

cdecl> cast p into pointer to int

cdecl> cast i into pointer to void

Read: man cdecl

HTH :)

On 8/10/05, Archana.S.R <archu.oct@gmail.com> wrote:
> Hi,
> 
> I started a LUG in Sri Ramakrishna Engg College by jan 2005 and still
> its a mail list
> This is the LUG iam talking about
> 
> http://groups.yahoo.com/group/srec-lug/
> [snip]
> -> wat is the benifit that the stud gets?

The main object of a Free Software User Group in a College would be to
introduce strudents to the Gnu/Linux Operating System, Free Software
Applications, insights into how Free Software projects are created,
maintained and distributed.  An understanding of these would make the
student a free software user, and may be encourage him/her to think of
a suitable final year project to fulfill both academic requirements,
and to exhibit skills learnt and acquired during the course.

> -> wat is the benifit that the college gets by having a LUG?

The reason for having a LUG in the first place is the availability of
Free Software. Many colleges are using proprietary software at the
moment, and they pay for the licenses through their nose. Many are
migrating to installing Free Software on all their systems, and as
that happens, a FSUG is merely a natural requirement.  The college
would save substantially on license fees, and besides, they have the
opportunity to teach better since free software comes with source
code.
 
> -> why LUG? 
> and similar other questions and monetary benifits too come before the
> authorities.

They must be knowing that:
Without LEarning there could be no Earning for professionals :)

FSUGs in colleges would mainly aid newbies  to learn about free
software that would be of use for the rest of their life.

> Iam sure that they wont allow if its just going be a
> discussion and teaching LUG since they hate to work for free, without
> any benifits.

That attitude suits unskilled labourers fine, but not professionals
who have a duty to encourage  students to learn and acquire useful
skills and knowledge.

If this is about earning directly from out of a FSUG, then, probably
the College could be charging small monthly subscriptions for
memberships to cover incidental expenses, if the rules allow for it.

HTH.
From base16 at gmail.com  Wed Aug 10 08:00:58 2005
From: base16 at gmail.com (Arvind Kalyan)
Date: Wed Aug 10 08:01:05 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Making SREC LUG active..
In-Reply-To: <87f4f642050809153030ac0544@mail.gmail.com>
References: <87f4f642050809153030ac0544@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <90c25f2705080919303e196740@mail.gmail.com>

On 8/10/05, Archana.S.R <archu.oct@gmail.com> wrote:

> -> wat is the benifit that the stud gets?
> -> wat is the benifit that the college gets by having a LUG?
> -> why LUG?

> My openions doesnt matter much there, so i need some kind of practical
> example in this regard.

> Anyone who would try to help me in this regard, please let me know wat
> can be done..

Linux-Advocacy HOWTO.

Back in 2002 I spent more than 4 months to get a base of 6 students
for backup. I also used this period to influence the college about the
advantages of Linux and others OSS products (like FreeBSD, etc).
Somehow they preferred to stay with Linux and the GNU base as it was
more userfriendly in their perspective. Also because of the hype from
the media.

I personally helped a whole department lab (EIE) to move onto Linux.
Gave them an environment they hadn't seen before (a simple NFS/NIS
network for whole of their department). Many were impressed. The heat
caught on. We introduced KLUG in Feb 2003. Students started coming in.
We had classes. We helped people move to Linux by being support
personnel.

And then it was not 'me' anymore. There were bunch of people who were
constantly using Linux. They were also willing to help others get used
to Linux which was misconceived as something difficult to use. To be
more precise, I helped a few of my class mates avoid using Win32 right
from second year so they are kind of uneasy when confronted with
Win32.

We conducted seminars, awareness programmes, quizzes, we celebrate
birthday of Linux kernel, etc.

To say the least - it was a process. It's not easy to impress the
management in a couple of hours, or even a day about the advantages of
OSS. If they are so aloof from the happenings of the IT industry, they
might be really hesitant for changes.

You might want to try going through Linux-Advocacy HOWTO. It tries to
help you in situations such as these.

regards,
-- 
Arvind Kalyan
http://www.devforge.net/~arv

Hi all,

I will offer a different perspective. I am not the typical LUG guy. I like 
Linux but also appreciate the effort that has gone into Windows (or any 
other end-user OS for that matter). What fascinates me at the end of the day 
is more the business side of things. I appreciate technology but I think 
more from an end-user point of view.


On 8/10/05, Archana.S.R <archu.oct@gmail.com> wrote:
> 
> > -> wat is the benifit that the stud gets?
> > -> wat is the benifit that the college gets by having a LUG?
> > -> why LUG?
> 
> 
Trying to answer your questions below - 
Lets think of the typical Linux business model. I know several companies 
exist that have gone the distro route but I a sure most of the business on 
the Linux end are services. When it comes down to services then it is people 
that matter. In today's information age we need intelligent, knowledgeable 
and versatile people and that too by the lakhs. Many say that the world is 
moving to an opensource era. So Linux is an essential tool for 
survival/improved prospects for the guys graduating now. 

Further, if the college strives for more money, the way they can do that is 
to have more students coming in and willing to pay the big bucks. And one 
way to that is to get more campus recruitments happening and colleges with 
an active LUG would probably appeal to corporates (especially in the Linux 
domain and even otherwise) because it shows the technology maturity of the 
students and indicates that they are not strait-jacketed to one technology 
only. And as someone else pointed out, adoption of free software might save 
them some bucks at the end of the day and they can have it maintained for 
free by the LUG if it is active. 

At the end of the day Linux just broadens your mind and introduces you to a 
whole new vibrant and fascinating community that is willing to share and 
grow together rather than a dog eat dog scenario typically found elsewhere.

HTH.

Deepak

On 8/9/05, Bhuvaneswaran A <bhuvaneswaran@gmail.com> wrote:
> > is successfully installed without any errors. But i
> > don't know how to activate the java. I have install
> 
> java:
> You should link libjavaplugin_oji.so to plugins sub-dir under mozilla
> installation. For example, if you have installed mozilla-firefox at
> /usr/lib/mozilla-firefox, you should copy this .so to
> /usr/lib/mozilla-firefox/plugins/ dir.
> 
> If you wish to enable it to a particular user alone, link it to
> $HOME/.mozilla/plugins dir. Alternatively, you can copy the .so file
> to the plugins dir. Finally, you should restart mozilla-firefox to
> enable it.
> 

No dont copy the plugin to the mozilla's plugin directory. It will
crash firefox. Instead create a soft link.

ln -s /usr/java/jre1.5.0_03/plugin/i386/ns7/libjavaplugin_oji.so
./libjavaplugin_oji.so

considering your java (jdk or jre) at /usr/java/....
Try this command from your mozilla's plugin dir.

For more info on installing/getting plugins for ffox in linux, check

http://plugindoc.mozdev.org/faqs/firefox-linux.html#install-java

V.Vishnu

Hi folks,

            Things are shaping up for Linux-Bangalore 2005 (the name may 
change soon), and a date has been announced for the event (29th Nov to

In office, I cant use Linux. I wanted to see the "Cath and Bazaar" tamil
version. I did the following and I was able to read it in my office M$
widoze m/c.

Copied the tamil unicode SooriyanDotCom.ttf from
http://www.sooriyan.com/font/ and put that in c:/winnt/fonts directory.

Copied the text(which ofcourse were mostly boxes) of the web page having
the tamil version of "cath and bazaar" and pasted in the M$ Word.

Selected the text and applied the newly put "SooriyanDotCom.ttf" font over
that.

Could now read the document in tamil in MS word/windows.

Some others who dont have access to Linux pc at office/xwindows can use
the above to read the web page.

Regards,
carti

From base16 at gmail.com  Wed Aug 10 17:06:23 2005
From: base16 at gmail.com (Arvind Kalyan)
Date: Wed Aug 10 17:06:40 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] Making SREC LUG active..
In-Reply-To: <87f4f64205081003592c879b5a@mail.gmail.com>
References: <266987a005080920035461b7bf@mail.gmail.com>
	<20050810034815.37626.qmail@web50208.mail.yahoo.com>

On 8/10/05, Archana.S.R <archu.oct@gmail.com> wrote:

> I thought he was there for 10 days for the training programme there.
> Since iam stil not in coimbatore iam not in a position to make that possible

Yes 10 days. I would have stayed if you wanted me too. May be next time :)

> Now i jus saw the srec-lug mail list and one of the studs there asked
> about the LUG thing to HOD and he was telling there was no lab
> technician to set up gnu/linux lab. Well i jus know the installation
> works. If any of you could jus help me with how to go around for the
> lab installation i can talk with HOD for the same.

Train a couple of students to take charge. They inturn will help the
technicians over a period of time.

Changing the operating systems in college labs should not be done in a
day or even a week. People seldom like large scale changes.

Couple of systems first. Then couple of systems in a couple of labs.
Make sure your 'crew' is very familiar with the most frequently
encountered issues. Then 'Linuxize' one of the labs completely,
tabulate the alternatives for the software expected in that lab (ie,
if it is C programming lab, have a notice of some sort that tells them
to use vi, gcc and tools with also the example commands)

Leave a gap of few days. During your LUG meet ask them what were the
issues the users (staff/students) faced. You can not expect all the
users to come to your LUG meet. So your 'crew' should visit the lab
once in a while and ask if there were any issues, note them down if
they themselves are not familiar with that situation. Then during the
meet the issues need to be discussed and solutions must be formulated
on printed material so that the staff can go through them at their
leisure.

Through out the various stages of migration, never talk to anyone with
the motive of eradicating Win32 - even if that thought lingers deep
within. Tell them how OSS is beneficial and let them decide if they
want to continue using Win32 or move on to OSS. This is the purpose of
awareness programmes. Please time them appropriately and have someone
experienced in these things to help you organize them if you are
concerned.

Apart from the above situation, there are quite a few issues you will
face while trying to migrate. Unless your college staff/students never
use the lab, it could be an ordeal to get the whole college know what
exactly is this Linux thing and to get linux installed even as a dual
boot.

Have a very crisp and clear objective why you want to move on to OSS.
The person or the bunch of people involved in this activities are
usually confronted with a lot of questions from many perspectives. So
to answer them without discrepencies in the stated objectives you must
be clear with the details. Frequent discussions with your mates and
outside people will come to your rescue at this point.

If you have even one person who is able to plan well and handle the
people's questions the right way, you should be able to infiltrate the
usage of OSS in your college.

After this comes your ability to handle people's problems. "Hey, I am
unable to install Linux on my computer! It doesn't work!" You can not
ask them to go online and read the man pages. Not every one is a
computer science engineer. If it is a EEE student, ask one of your CSE
juniors to help them. Delegation is essential. When you give someone a
bit of responsibility, they feel recognized and important. Ultimately
they will try spending more time in learning and trying to help. They
will start frequenting LUG meets to be able to handle future problems.

What I mean is, after this point it is your leadership qualities that
will bring in a momentum. A little bit of it is enough. Then the
students will catch up.


All the best,

-- 
Arvind Kalyan
http://www.devforge.net/~arv
From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Wed Aug 10 17:38:40 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)
Date: Wed Aug 10 17:38:56 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Fedora Core 4: Another mini-review
Message-ID: <a8f990120508100508764aaafe@mail.gmail.com>

Hi folks,
            I just upgraded an existing FC3 installation on a Dell Inspiron
P3/700 notebook to FC4, and here are my first impressions after playing
with it for about a day:

1. It is faster than FC3 in most areas: Booting to the login prompt, X
    startup, text scrolling within xterm, general desktop responsiveness,
    system shutdown. About 10-30% quicker overall, which is nothing 
    short of miraculous - given that this comes for free, and seems to be
    rock stable (so far).

2. Everything 'just worked' in my upgrade installation, except the audio
   (maestro3). I had to manually tweak /etc/modprobe.conf to get alsa to
    recognise the audio (perhaps it might have worked perfectly if I'd
    done a fresh install instead of an upgrade).

3. Existing binary RPMs from FC3 will mostly work on FC4 with minimal
    dependency problems - the situation is reminiscent of the transition
    from RH 7.3 to RH 8, but without the hairy bugs. 

4.  The gcc-4.0.0 compiler is more picky and will generate fresh errors
    that were undetected by gcc-3.4.x. Therefore, some earlier SRPMs
    and kernels will not build on an FC4 host with gcc4. For instance, 
     Linux-2.6.8.1, abiword-2.0.12-9 and xmms-1.2.7-21 all broke during
    build. However, Linux-2.6.12 (from kernel.org) compiles fine and I 
    replaced the FC4 kernel with this one, with no apparent problems.

5. Since binary RPMs built on FC3 install fine on FC4, it's a good idea
    to have an FC3 build machine with gcc-3.4.x for building earlier RPMs
    and kernels.
    
6. The only Cons of FC4: the relative immaturity of the gcc4 toolchain, 
    and the larger memory footprint (256 MB recommended for FC4 vs.
    128 MB for FC3).

7.  Overall, I'd rate this distro 9/10 - the main Pros are speed, ease of
    migration, API stability, ABI stability. It's great for breathing new
    life into aging hardware (for reference, the difference in performance
    between a P3/1Ghz and a Northwood Celeron 2.4 GHz is about 25%
    for gcc-3.4 compilation of Firefox. We could get this same boost 
    for free by upgrading from FC3 to FC4 on the P3/1GHz.)

To summarize: Everything just works as before, only quicker. Go for it!

-Siva

P.S. My pam-losetup/cryptoloop stuff still works, with on-disk binary 
compatibility retained from Linux-2.4/RH 7.3. Try doing these kinds of 
things with NTFS or similar crap in the M$ world.

On 8/10/05, Frederick Noronha (FN) <fred@bytesforall.org> wrote:

> meet requesting for comments (RFC) on TUNE, Tamil Unicode -- New.
> 
> The Tamil Virtual University and Kanithamizh Sangam (Association for
> Tamil Computing) will organise the event on Wednesday, August 10, 2005
> between 11 am and 1 pm at the Days Inn Deccan Plaza, 36 Royapettah High

> 
> C Chandramouli, IAS, Secretary, Department of IT of the Government of
> Tamil Nadu, will release the TUNE Toolkit. Programme includes a welcome

Thanks for the info. I attended the meeting and it turned out to be
very informative. This was the official meeting where TUNE - Tamil Unicode New,
RFC was launched. The rationale for a new standard was explained very
articulately by a Prof. Krishnamoorthy from Crescent college - he
explained how current efforts try to shoehorn Tamil into a design by committee
standards, and why that doesn't work well. A "free as in Rasna" CD
containing documentation, fonts, sample files, etc was given to the
participants. The CD included OpenOffice for Windows and Mac, but not Linux.
The TUNE folks are looking for volunteer testers and have estimated the
initial testing period to hundred days. They have also set up a Yahoo
groups where TUNE can be discussed.

TUNE essentially is a thumbs down to efforts like the current Tamil
Unicode, and ISCII  where little input was taken from folks actually
knowledgeable in Tamil or the
nuances of the language, and is a total home grown effort from folks at
TVU (Tamil Virtual University) and Kanithamizh Sangam.

Ramaswamy

Dear Ramaswamy,
Is there any open website where information related to this TUNE is
available.  (not closed yahoogroups ).

IMHO , The current tamil unicode is working well and there is no need
for any new encoding.

This TUNE effort should not be encouraged. This will only bring down
the current momentum of tamil computing works drastically.

If we look back, some of the current members of Kanithamiz Sangam were
responsible for creating alternate encodings in the year 1999 called
TAM & TAB.

It should be noted, TSCII was in use much earlier (i think from 1998 onwards). 
TSCII was a discussed in openforum (hosted by tamil.net those days)
for nearly a year and formed as a open 8-bit standard.

But some of the Commercial Tamil software Vendors based in Tamil Nadu
with the help of then DMK government created & announced TAB/TAM. It
should be noted, this TAB/TAM efforts were not open and were formed
without taking into consideration TSCII - the open 8-bit Tamil
standard available in those days.

TAB/TAM efforts almost killed the momemtum of tamil computing in those
TSCII days by creating confusion among the developers.
Nowadays only Tamil Nadu Govt websites are having TAB/TAM encoding. It
doesnt enjoy much support among users and Developers.

I find similar thing is going to happen now...

Now we have a working Tamil unicode encoding. 
And tamil unicode is gaining acceptance among the tamil computer users
, developers, Major Software Vendors & Freesoftware community.

At this critical moment, there is absolutely no need for any new Tamil
UNICODE encoding.

Only few in the Tamil Nadu - ** that too mostly Comercial Tamil
software vendors** under Kanithamizh sangam,  are attempting to create
an alternate tamil New encoding with the help of govt agencies.

Current unicode DOES NOT HAVE ANY PROBLEM, This new Tamil unicode
encoding by commercial software vendors , should be prevented at any
cost.

[
For more info abt TSCII Refer:
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TSCII
http://www.tamil.net/tscii/
http://www.geocities.com/Athens/5180/tscii.html
]

Regards,
Mugunth

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Aug 10 20:45:29 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Aug 10 20:44:59 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (C++DECL)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0508102013210.16449-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Tamil Language WikiPedia: http://ta.wikipedia.org/

One Day One Command 
===================

c++decl -- Create/Explain C++ Type Declarations.

Summary:

Cdecl is a program for encoding and decoding C/C++ type declarations
in English language. Both cdecl and c++decl are same program. cdecl
will use C notation and c++decl use C++. It can run in interactive
(shell-like) and non-interactive mode (command line arguments).

In the interactive mode, cdecl will wait for your input in "c++decl> " 
prompt. Enter "quit or exit" to exit. Enter "?" for help.

Examples:

$ c++decl -- Start the c++decl in interactive mode.

c++decl> quit -- Exit c++decl.

c++decl> declare i as static integer 

c++decl> declare x as reference to pointer to character

c++decl> declare foo as pointer to member of class X int

c++decl> explain class Y *(X::*foo)(arg1, arg2)

$ c++decl -c declare signal as function returning int -- Create 
                            compilable C or C++ code as output.

Read: man c++decl

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

> the current momentum of tamil computing works drastically.
> 
> If we look back, some of the current members of Kanithamiz Sangam were
> responsible for creating alternate encodings in the year 1999 called
> TAM & TAB.
> 
> It should be noted, TSCII was in use much earlier (i think from 1998 onwards).
> TSCII was a discussed in openforum (hosted by tamil.net those days)
> for nearly a year and formed as a open 8-bit standard.
> 
> But some of the Commercial Tamil software Vendors based in Tamil Nadu
> with the help of then DMK government created & announced TAB/TAM. It
> should be noted, this TAB/TAM efforts were not open and were formed
> without taking into consideration TSCII - the open 8-bit Tamil
> standard available in those days.
> 
> TAB/TAM efforts almost killed the momemtum of tamil computing in those
> TSCII days by creating confusion among the developers.
> Nowadays only Tamil Nadu Govt websites are having TAB/TAM encoding. It
> doesnt enjoy much support among users and Developers.
> 
> I find similar thing is going to happen now...
> 
> Now we have a working Tamil unicode encoding.
> And tamil unicode is gaining acceptance among the tamil computer users
> , developers, Major Software Vendors & Freesoftware community.
> 
> At this critical moment, there is absolutely no need for any new Tamil
> UNICODE encoding.
> 
> Only few in the Tamil Nadu - ** that too mostly Comercial Tamil
> software vendors** under Kanithamizh sangam,  are attempting to create
> an alternate tamil New encoding with the help of govt agencies.
> 
> Current unicode DOES NOT HAVE ANY PROBLEM, This new Tamil unicode
> encoding by commercial software vendors , should be prevented at any
> cost.
> 

Mugunth, 

Other than the Yahoo news group "tune_rfc" they didn't mention any
other links/resources. The presentations seem to have been uploaded to
the Yahoo group (tune_rfc). Check out the documents there. Looks like
you need moderator approval before you can join the group.

Ramaswamy

about linux and its righteousness in giving solution. As my client's
only task is to check emails , download some files in the attachment

> > -> wat is the benifit that the college gets by having a LUG?
> 
> The reason for having a LUG in the first place is the availability of
> Free Software. Many colleges are using proprietary software at the
> moment, and they pay for the licenses through their nose. Many are
Hmm.. still most of the software in our college labs are pirated.. (I
had to put up a fight to let them let me use Java instead of pirated
versions of VB, though I had to give reasons like "Java is truly
object oriented and related nonsense")

> opportunity to teach better since free software comes with source

Hmm.. I know that I am speaking for majority of the students of engg.
college's here when I say that 'Teach better since free software comes
with source' is an extremely fallacious argument.. because, many of
them equate the free in 'Free Software' to free beer, not free speech.

And secondly, most of them are not even interested in looking at
further references to 'clearly explain concepts', let alone go and
check out under the hood of a compiler or an Operating System.

Even, with the source, most mature  Free/Open Source software (that
are usually bundled with distro's) are not very good teaching tools,
as the pack too much complexity, and simple ones are well.. too simple
to learn anything useful. The middle ground is hard to find.

Maybe I phrased it wrong, but.. here is what I tried to say..
I said mature tools, for eg,  GCC is a really bad place to learn
compiler design, kernel 2.6.12 is a bad place to start learning about
"OS scheduling algorithms"(maybe 0.0.1, but not 2.6) . I am talking
about this kinda thing.. well you can always try out other simpler
compilers out there..and it might still be FLOSS, but you've to search
for it. So, that argument about 'FLOSS is a great place to learn about
CS' and hence ' I shall go forth and install debian sarge'  do not
follow each other logically.. thats what I meant to say..  take for
example, a good place to start compiler design would be to look into
very simple implementations of languages without too much of a syntax
etc.. how many run of the mill distro's provide that?

But still thats no reason, not to go ahead and use the argument for
starting a LUG or spreading any form of linux awareness.

Sure. But, it is no excuse for students not to take
the initiative and learn. We can only bring the horse
to the pond, can't force it to drink the water. Even
if the students are given the best lectures, and if
they don't open up their minds and listen, there isn't
much one can do.
 
Even HR training will be on group dynamics, group
games, blah blah blah. If it has to be technical, they
will ask the campus college staff themselves to teach.
So, its not going to be any different from what
students have studied (as opposed to learning).

> Maybe I phrased it wrong, but.. here is what I tried
> to say..
> I said mature tools, for eg,  GCC is a really bad
> place to learn
> compiler design, 

lex, yacc, flex, bison?

http://ds9a.nl/lex-yacc/

> kernel 2.6.12 is a bad place to
> start learning about
> "OS scheduling algorithms"(maybe 0.0.1, but not 2.6)

It doesn't have to be 2.6.12. It can be any 2.6
kernel. 

Operating systems is an ocean by itself. There are
definitely a lot of dependent concepts and components
to it. Nobody will straight away ask you to take the
course. That is why students are first introduced to
algorithms, complexity, data structures, computer
systems,  microprocessors and then operating systems.
You build on the former.

Understanding the Linux Kernel: Process Scheduling:
http://www.oreilly.com/catalog/linuxkernel/chapter/ch10.html

Software revolution documentation on the Linux kernel:
http://www.softwarerevolution.com/jeneral/open-source-docs.html

Linux kernel cross-reference:
http://lxr.linux.no

Nobody is going to teach you in the industry. There is
a lot of competition. The ability to read RFCs and
specifications, comprehend them and implement them is
important. This methodology must start from colleges.
Unfortunately, students are spoon-fed and they are not
made to use their brain cells.

Just my thoughts,

SK

From mbchandar at gmail.com  Thu Aug 11 08:00:45 2005
From: mbchandar at gmail.com (bala chandar)
Date: Thu Aug 11 08:00:56 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT]Some Tips for your Business
Message-ID: <dc538c3f05081019303f9e779e@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

You cannot change all of a sudden in the users mind. End user always
has a mind to choose is comfortablity. His mind have been fully loaded
with windows and its environment. His Neighbours would change his mind
and ask him to use windows and they might also said Linux is tough to
use.

I suggest you go with the little.... 

migrate the user's browser from IE to Firefox
migrate Thunderbird browser from Outlook Express to Thunderbird
migrate Outlook Calendar to Sunbird
migrate windows media player to xine / mplayer / xmms
migrate yahoo/msn msgr to windows gaim msgr
migrate Norton Antivirus to AVG Free Antivirus Edition

Tell the features of these softwares to the user and let him migrate
to these. and slowly migrate MS Office to Open Office v2.

In this way you can say the user how FLOSS is good to use and easy to
use with no cost....Also introduce him to some projects from source
forge so that he can use it for his purpose.....

once you did all this.. it is easy for the user to understand about
FLOSS and Linux OS. then you easily migrate the user to Linux OS from
windows. also show some demo using Knoppix/Mandriva Move....

Subject: [Ilugc] ur reliance problems

hi,
heres a trick that worked for my tata indicom, reinstall the existing 
installation and check for the files wvdial.conf and resolv.conf, browse 
the internet for a few minutes and restart the computer , check whether 
the files have been changed, this happens when u boot up with ur phone 
connected to the pc, so connect ur phone only after the welcome screen, 
also download webmin from http://www.webmin.com  and install it, now in 
the networking section there will be a ppp dialup client link, u can 
connect from there too. the reason is webmin provides u with a nice gui 
in a browser to manage all ur system tasks

regards,
Sudharshan S

Distribution dependant and "/proc/config.gz" dependant.

> also download webmin from http://www.webmin.com  and install it, now in
> the networking section there will be a ppp dialup client link, u can
> connect from there too. the reason is webmin provides u with a nice gui

This is an overkill. Seriously, for a personal computer. Ultimately
you will not learn anything about configuration. And you will try
installing webmin when ever people ask you to help them configure
their systems.

But yes, for large scale installations webmin and cousins might help.
Not for a personal computer.

Even though software is free of cost, it will be nice if we learnt to
use the right ones at the right time. I'm assuming you are a Computer
Engineer, if that is not the case, by all means you may please ignore
this e-mail.

I havent executed the command, as far as my understanding, SSH connection is
asking for password.
You can use three way of authentication for SSH

1. Key authentication.
		two options (without user intervention)
			(i) pulic key with empty passphrase.
			(ii) using SSH agent
2. password authentication. --> ruled out 
3. Host authentication.

From binand at gmail.com  Fri Aug 12 03:14:21 2005

Date: Fri Aug 12 12:44:31 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Help in MySQL
In-Reply-To: <loom.20050812T054536-55@post.gmane.org>
References: <loom.20050812T054536-55@post.gmane.org>
Message-ID: <d2a92d6105081200145b2dc12e@mail.gmail.com>

On 11/08/05, Aravindakshan M R <digivind@rediffmail.com> wrote:
> Can anybody pls tell, how do i connect 2 tables with foreign key using common
> fields.....
> If i delete one row on table 1 then it should automatically cascaded with a
> deletion of the corresponding row in table 2.....
> pls tell a solution soon

Which version of MySQL? Until 5.x somewhere, MySQL didn't support
foreign keys (and it called itself a SQL database ;)

The syntax would be:

create table mytable (
    somefield int4,
    constraint somefield_valid foreign key (somefield) references
someothertable(itsfield) on delete cascade
);

Binand

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Aug 12 20:53:25 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Aug 12 20:52:24 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (CHVT)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0508122024590.16939-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

The Assayer is the web's largest catalog of free books, most of them
in Creative Commons license, and also collects user-submitted reviews.
URL: http://theassayer.org/ (Thanks Anand)

One Day One Command 
===================

chvt -- CHange foreground Virtual Terminal.

Summary:

In GNU/Linux OS, be default, 6 virtual text mode console terminals
will be running. User can switch between this terminals using Left 
Side Ctrl + Alt + FunKey(1 - 6).

chvt command is also used to switch between this terminals. It can 
be used in shell scripts.

Examples:

$ chvt 1 -- Switch from current terminal to /dev/tty1.

$ chvt 2 -- Switch from current terminal to /dev/tty2.

Read: man chvt

TIP: Screen Dump in Text console.

# sudo cat /dev/vcs2 > scrdump.txt  -- Take the screen dump of 
                                 /dev/tty2 in scrdump.txt file.

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From p_mdriyaz at fastmail.fm  Fri Aug 12 21:03:09 2005
From: p_mdriyaz at fastmail.fm (Mohammed Riyaz)
Date: Fri Aug 12 21:03:29 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] help needed for configuring my mfd
In-Reply-To: <42FC4FFC.3090206@gmail.com>
References: <42FC4FFC.3090206@gmail.com>
Message-ID: <1123860789.3306.240559915@webmail.messagingengine.com>

Hi,

On Fri, 12 Aug 2005 13:00:04 +0530, "Sudharshan S" <sudharsh@gmail.com>
said:

> i have a hp psc 1315 mfd with a scanner and a copier, i downloaded the 
> hp device manger. but my device ids not getting detected, it keeps 
> giving a message that i have to install the device with the cups 
> backend, what does that mean.

If you had installed cups without any prefix then if u look into
/usr/share/cups/backend you should find a couple of backend programs
which transport the print job from cups to the particular device. like
usb or parallel port etc. So from what you say i guess it is telling you
to register a new backend provided with your hp driver in the backend
folder. This could mean simply copying the corresponding backend program
into the backend folder and then restart cups for it to detect the new
backed.

HTH.

Mohammed Riyaz.

-- 
http://www.fastmail.fm - A fast, anti-spam email service.

Automake and Autoconf are the tools using which we can create scripts 
necessary to run the configure, make and make install commands that we use 
to install softwares in linux. If some one is developing a software in linux 
then this talk will tell him how to make a tarball of that software. The 
talk will only introduce you to these tools. I will soon mail a Abstract of 
the talk.

Hi,

--- bala murugan <balakec@yahoo.co.in> wrote:
> Though, i am able to establish a connection by
> running adsl-start (found it out  by checking the
> /var/log/messages shows the session id,local and
> remote ip addresses),  

You check your network status from the output of:

/sbin/ifconfig -a

Post the output. Does it show a ppp0 entry?

> I am not able to browse. I
> tried pinging to google, but only in vain. 

You first try to ping an IP address.

1. See if you can ping your DNS server(s).
2. Ping an IP address, say, 66.94.230.46
3. Post the file contents of /etc/resolv.conf

On Sun, 14 Aug 2005 11:46:49 +0530, Aravindakshan  
<digivind@rediffmail.com> wrote:

> Can anyone give me a clear picture of waht is mambo?

It is a content management system (CMS) which helps you
create/maintain dynamic content driven website/portals
efficiently. There are many other CMS (each of them are
good in their own way).

Check out http://www.cmsmatrix.org/ to explore/evaluate
other CMS suite. If you want to know more about mambo
server, try the following links:
   http://www.mamboserver.com/
   http://www.mamboportal.com/
   http://www.mamboforge.net/

A google search for "mambo server" should show up many links.

--
Chandrashekar Babu.
http://www.chandrashekar.info/

hi,
here is how u do it,
first make sure u have php, apache or any of the database server (i use 
mysql for my mambo sites)
i assume u have already installed php and apache, if not let me know and 
i will walk you through the installation.
u MUST have apache installed and properly configured to load the php 
modules to run mambo sites locally

heres a tip to save ur bandwidth costs!!!

download phpmyadmin and backup the database containing ur  mambo site. 
ur hosting account should have provided u a database and some tool to 
manage. using this tool u can sync both the database nad hence u need 
not spend hours modifying ur site. dont forget u need apache or similar 
webserver.
let me know if u have any other doubts

From deepan.chakravarthy at gmail.com  Mon Aug 15 01:45:41 2005
From: deepan.chakravarthy at gmail.com (Deepan Chakravarthy N)
Date: Mon Aug 15 01:45:51 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Abstract for "AUTOMAKE and AUTOCONF"...
Message-ID: <2453a9a205081413154be3403a@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Shakthi and others..
Here is the summary of what i expect to cover.. Comments are welcome. I 
might change the order or contents later if needed.

Topic: AUTOMAKE and AUTOCONF

1)Introduction to autotools.. 
why they exist.. 
how it helps programmers and users..
2)Introduction to makefiles.. 
use of makefiles
3)requirements on both developers and users machine..
4)basic organisation of automake and autoconf.
5)the basic steps involved in creating a source tarball.
6)how to write basic configure.in <http://configure.in> and
makefile.am<http://makefile.am>scripts
7)how to check for presence of libraries.
8)how to check for the presence of headers..
9)how to write man pages
10)how to pass compiler and linker options
11)how to create a tar ball 
12)user groups.. irc and other important links



--

final year ,B.Tech,

Anna University,
Chennai.

hi,
heres my phone number, 55377718
its gr8 i was of help to you. ok here's mambo indepth.
first of all u need not know anything about php. u must have downloaded 
mambo tarball.
extract the whole folder locally. ftp the contents directly to ur 
webspace. suppose ur contents are extracted to './mambo/' extract THIS 
directory as it. say u have uploaded the contents to 
<ur_webspace>/mambo, point ur browser to http://<ur_webspace>/mambo. u 
must be welcomed by a installation screen. now ur webhost must have 
provided u with a database. be sure to include ur database name and set 
the host to localhost. thats it! remember to chmod the approriate files 
and folders especially the configuration.php file to world executable, u 
can do that in ur ftp client itself. now as i had mentioned design ur 
site locally and synchronize the database. if u encounter any problems, 
let me know

cheers,
Sudharshan S
From sudharsh at gmail.com  Mon Aug 15 20:08:26 2005
From: sudharsh at gmail.com (Sudharshan S)
Date: Mon Aug 15 21:04:00 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] about mambo and its association with php
Message-ID: <4300A8E2.2050609@gmail.com>

hi,
sorry bout the fact that i didnt read ur reply correctly. i suppose u r 
having the doubt about php in mambo.
php, as u must be knowing is a webscripting language like java or asp, 
the catch is u dont need any extra software to run php scripts on ur 
system unlike java which requires some kind of software which in this 
case is JVM or Java Virtual Machine. View the source of a php page from 
ur browser and u will find only html tags! this is bcause php embeds 
within html. All this is done on the Server itself, unlike in java where 
the actual interpretation occurs on the client i.e. the users' system. 
Now mambo uses php because of its close association with MySQL and they 
are quite good chums. Suppose u were to submit some form information in 
mambo. what it actually does is get ur form data, create approriate 
tables in MySQL database. also when u register in a mambo based site it 
creates tables for the  approriate fields like passwords, address. etc. 
now since php n MySQL are closely related all this is seamless and 
nothing is visible to the user. and remember php iand MySQL (to sum 
extent) are open source. moreover php is lightweight and doesnt require 
any software to be installed on the client side. so it pretty natural 
that a CMS like mambo to use php.

Hey theres another cms called mamboplus derived from mambo itself. the 
catch is it also includes a phpBB forum with it and moreover ur users 
can login in the forums and the websites with the same user id, separate 
registration for the forums is not required. if u have any doubts just 
give me a call to 55377718 anytime and i'll be glad to help

gnully,
Sudharshan S

From ramanraj.k at gmail.com  Mon Aug 15 20:21:15 2005
From: ramanraj.k at gmail.com (Ramanraj K)
Date: Mon Aug 15 21:20:17 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Suggestions to the Draft Manual of Patent Practice and
	Procedure
Message-ID: <f480bf1e05081507511e6e7006@mail.gmail.com>

The Patent Office, India, has published a DRAFT MANUAL  OF PATENT
PRACTICE & PROCEDURE (2005) at
http://www.patentoffice.nic.in/ipr/patent/manual-2052005.pdf and has
also invited suggestions to correct the draft.  Our main concern would
be Annexure II, that deals with EXAMINATION  GUIDELINES FOR
PATENTABILITY OF COMPUTER-RELATED INVENTIONS and all portions
incidental thereto in the Draft Manual, which is largely ultra vires
the Patents Act and the TRIPs Treaty.  A draft representation is
posted at:

http://mm.gnu.org.in/pipermail/fsf-friends/2005-August/003476.html

Please post your comments, if any, asap.

Thanks,
Ramanraj.
