Bharathi S

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Mon Aug 29 21:16:42 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Mon Aug 29 21:15:51 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (OGGINFO)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0508292059120.30649-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Since 1998, Linux Weekly News (LWN) has been covering the Linux & Free
Software communities development activites in a concise, well-written,
and objective manner. URL: http://lwn.net/

One Day One Command 
===================

ogginfo -- Gives information about Ogg files.

Summary:

Ogg Vorbis is a new audio compression format. It is different from
these other formats because it is completely free, open & unpatented.
It is roughly comparable to other formats used to store & play digital
music, such as MP3, VQF, AAC, and other digital audio formats.

ogginfo reads one or more Ogg files and prints information about
stream contents. It will detect (but not correct)  a wide range of
common defects, with many additional checks specifically for Ogg
Vorbis streams.

Examples:

$ locate .ogg -- Search for some OGG files in your system.

$ ogginfo /usr/share/redhat-credits.ogg -- Show the detailed info 
                                           about that ogg file.

$ ogginfo -q /usr/share/redhat-credits.ogg -- Show warning and errors
                                              messages.

$ ogginfo -qq /usr/share/redhat-credits.ogg -- Show only errors. 

Read: man ogginfo

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From sudharsh at gmail.com  Mon Aug 29 21:28:25 2005
From: sudharsh at gmail.com (Sudharshan S)
Date: Mon Aug 29 21:28:13 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] (no subject)
Message-ID: <431330A1.3020104@gmail.com>

hello,
sir u must change the following lines

>[Modem0]
>Modem = /dev/modem
>  
>
the above line to 'Modem = /dev/ttySL0'. this is the location of your modem.

>Baud = 57600
>
the above line refers to the speed with which you are connecting

>SetVolume = 1
>Dial Command = ATDT
>Init1 = ATZ
>Init3 = ATM1L1
>FlowControl = CRTSCTS
>  
>
>[Dialer BSNL]
>Username = purelife
>Password = uma579
>Phone = 172233
>Stupid Mode = 1
>Init1 = ATZ
>Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0
>Inherits = Modem0
>
>[Dialer Defaults]
>Modem = /dev/ttySL0
>Baud = 460800
>  
>
try changing this to 'Baud = 57600' .because 460800 is too high for a 56 
kbps dialup modem

>Init1 = ATZ
>Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0
>ISDN = 0
>Modem Type = Analog Modem
> Phone = 172233
> Username = purelife
> Password = uma579
>Carrier Check = No
>Stupid Mode = On
>
Now issue
'wvdial BSNL' or 'wvdial Defaults'
Make sure you had entered the correct ip address in the resolv.conf file 
found in /etc/
Note: please do change your password asap, u have exposed it. Let us 
know if this worked right

regards and good luck
Sudharshan S

From siva.ilugc at gmail.com  Tue Aug 30 07:43:16 2005
From: siva.ilugc at gmail.com (Sivasankar Chander)

Subject: [Ilugc] Heads up: Linksys WRT54G available locally (OpenWRT capable)
Message-ID: <a8f990120508291913408ddc22@mail.gmail.com>

Folks,
The Linksys WRT54G Wireless B/G WiFi/Broadband Router/AP is
available locally at Ritchie Street for ~Rs.4k (YMMV, shop around).
This is a fairly decent price for the earliest/best such product in the
market.

The main advantage is that it uses an embedded Linux distro based
on busybox, uclibc, etc., and a fully open-source alternative called
OpenWRT can be flashed on it to improve its features, including
adding support for community mesh networking, etc.

Do a Google search for 'WRT54G Linux' to understand its features.

-Siva

On Tue, 30 Aug 2005, vikram balaji wrote:

> Is there any software available for converting an existing Mp3
> format audio into Ogg vorbis?

AFAIK, there is no tool avail to directly convert from MP3 to OGG.
Usual method is MP3 -> WAV -> OGG (see the example). In this method,
output quality will be reduced. For best result for convert the
original WAV file to OGG.

mpg123 my.mp3 -w - | oggenc -o my.ogg -

Bye :)
-- 
Bharathi S

This is a little OT from the above, but yet connected:

Fredrick P Brooks wrote in the Mythical Man-month:

"One of the most impressive developments in software during the past
two decades has been the truimph of the Windows, Icons, Menus,
Pointing interface - or WIMP for short.  It is today so familiar as to
need no description.  This concept was first publicly displayed by
Doug Englebart and his team from the Stanford Research Institute at
the Western Joint Computer Conference of 1968.  From there the ideas
went to Xerox Palo Alto ....."

The screens of today are too small in pixels to show details and the
"so-called 'desktop metaphor' of today's workstation is instead an
'airplane-seat' metaphor.  Anyone who has shuffled a lapful of papers
while seated in coach between two portly passengers will recognize the
difference - one can seen only a very few things at once.  The true
desktop provides overview of and random access to a score of pages
..."

Now:
[1] We have projectors and therefore more real estate should be
possible the "Desktop" (imagine a real 4 feet x 2 feet "Desktop"). 
What XF86Config would suit this end?  Would it be possible for X to
use one config for the laptop screen and another for the projector?

[2] Computer monitors are the most serious health hazard to the
environment. While used, they emit a fair amount of radiation (enough
to advise preg. women to stay away from them during pregnancy) and
even the more modern LCD screens are either expensive or not as
convenient as a projector.  If any of you are hardware engineers,
please think of mnf. web cam sized projectors, that could render a
decent 4' x 2' screen, that may be cheap, affordable, and may be even
bring the price of computers to less than Rs. 5000/-
 
-Ramanraj.

> [1] We have projectors and therefore more real estate should be
> possible the "Desktop" (imagine a real 4 feet x 2 feet "Desktop").
> What XF86Config would suit this end? Would it be possible for X to
> use one config for the laptop screen and another for the projector?


Yes, but the actual resolution of most projectors is no more than
XGA (1024x768). This is not as good as many high-end notebooks
with SXGA (1440 x 1080) or higher resolutions.

There are high-end projectors for digital cinema applications that
have resolutions as high as 3072 X 2048 (or even higher), but these
are very expensive - not less than $250k or Rs. 1 crore / unit.

[2] If any of you are hardware engineers,
> please think of mnf. web cam sized projectors, that could render a
> decent 4' x 2' screen, that may be cheap, affordable, and may be even
> bring the price of computers to less than Rs. 5000/-
> 
> Small projectors do exist, but they aren't that inexpensive - the least
expensive DLP projectors are ~Rs.50k today, which is a fraction of the
price at which DLP was originally introduced ~20 years ago. Acer has
such a low-end DLP projector available in India now.

-Siva

From marvstod at comcast.net  Sun Aug 28 16:52:06 2005
From: marvstod at comcast.net (marvstod@comcast.net)
Date: Tue Aug 30 19:35:45 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Agere soft Modem on Acer Laptop 4152NLCi
Message-ID: <082820051652.15864.4311EBB6000496EB00003DF822007614380B019B9C909D0E03@comcast.net>

RAM

RE:   ./slmodem -alsa -c INDIA hw:1
should be:
   ./slmodemd --alsa -c INDIA hw:1
or
   ./slmodemd   -a -c INDIA hw: 1

Note that you can 
# su - root
# cp  slmodemd  /usr/bin/
putting slmodemd on the COMMAND PATH.  Thereafter it will suffice to:
# slmodemd --alsa -c INDIA hw:1 

See if using --alsa cures the problem

Also your /etc/wvdial.conf  looks as if was produced by first running the ICW and then the last section was appended by a:  wvdialconf /etc/wvdial.conf
This may be causing a problem  You can however for testing run.  
# wvdialconf wvtest.txt

To correct the /etc/wvdial.conf, do
# cp /etc/wvdial.conf  /etc/wvdial.conf.0
and then edit /etc/wvdial.conf  into the following:

[Modem0]
Modem = /dev/ttySL0
Baud = 57600
SetVolume = 1
Dial Command = ATDT
Init1 = ATZ
Init3 = ATM1L1
FlowControl = CRTSCTS
Carriier Check = no

[Dialer BSNL]
Username = purelife
Password = uma579
Phone = 172233
Stupid Mode = 1
Init2 = ATQ0 V1 E1 S0=0 &C1 &D2 +FCLASS=0
# Once there is a success, try commenting out the following line, which is a ICW default
Stupid Mode = On
Inherits = Modem0

For usage of KPPP, it is probably necessary to first run its setup, This must be done as a User too, not just by root

Report back presently.

MarvS

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Tue Aug 30 19:56:59 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Tue Aug 30 19:55:51 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (OGG123)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0508301935430.15102-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

Since 1998, Linux Weekly News (LWN) has been covering the Linux & Free
Software communities development activites in a concise, well-written,
and objective manner. URL: http://lwn.net/

One Day One Command 
===================

ogg123 -- Plays Ogg Vorbis audio files.

Summary:

Ogg Vorbis is a new audio compression format. It is different from
these other formats because it is completely free, open & unpatented.
It is roughly comparable to other formats used to store & play digital
music, such as MP3, VQF, AAC, and other digital audio formats.

ogg123 reads Ogg Vorbis audio files and decodes/play them to the (by
default) standard sound card or specified device(s). Input files can
be read from the system, or URLs can be streamed via HTTP.

Press Ctrl C to stop.

Examples:

$ locate .ogg -- Search for some OGG files in your system.

$ ogg123 my.ogg -- Play on the default soundcard.

$ ogg123 -q my.ogg -- Quiet mode. No messages are displayed.

$ ogg123 -v my.ogg -- Verbose mode. Show more info.

$ ogg123 -x 4 my.ogg -- Play the file in 4 time faster.

$ ogg123 -y 2 my.ogg -- Play the file in 2 times slower then the 
                        normal speed.

$ ogg123 -d esd my.ogg -- Play the file using ESD Device.

$ ogg123 ~/MusicDir -- Play  all of the files in the ~/MusicDir
                       and its subDirs.

$ ogg123 -d wav -f my.wav my.ogg -- Convert the OGG to WAV.

$ ogg123 -d oss -d wav -f my.wav my.ogg -- Listen to a file while you
                                           write it to a WAV file.

Read: man ogg123 (More examples are available in man page)

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Wed Aug 31 22:44:09 2005
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Wed Aug 31 22:42:45 2005
Subject: [Ilugc] One Day One Command (OGGENC)
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0508312207330.14279-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

RUTE User's Tutorial and Exposition, One of best free book for 
GNU/Linux. URL: http://web.whittier.edu/jlutgen/rute/rute.html

One Day One Command 
===================

oggenc -- Encode audio into the Ogg Vorbis format.

Summary:

Ogg Vorbis is a new audio compression format. It is different from
these other formats because it is completely free, open & unpatented.
It is roughly comparable to other formats used to store & play digital
music, such as MP3, VQF, AAC, and other digital audio formats.

oggenc reads audio data in either raw, WAV or AIFF format and encodes
it into an Ogg Vorbis stream. 

Examples:

$ locate .wav -- Search for some WAV files in your system.

$ oggenc snd.wav -- Produces output as snd.ogg.

$ oggenc in.wav -o out.ogg -- Produces output as out.ogg.

$ oggenc in.wav -q 6 -o out.ogg -- Produces the output with specified 
                         quality, -1 (low) & 10 (high), 3 is default.

$ oggenc snd.wav -t "MyTrack1" -a "MyName" -l "MySound" -o snd.ogg --
                                   Add Track info in the output file.

Read: man oggenc

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S
ODOC LJ -- http://www.livejournal.com/community/ilugc/
